<div id="review_1952629301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952629301" />
    <a title="Kris - My Novelesque Life" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life"><img alt="Kris - My Novelesque Life" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577743166p2/6275022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1952629301?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris - My Novelesque Life" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris - My Novelesque Life" href="/user/show/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life">Kris - My Novelesque Life</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life?shelf=britain">britain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life?shelf=made-into-a-tv-series">made-into-a-tv-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6275022-kris---my-novelesque-life?shelf=saga">saga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1952629301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6458188073118304179">I am a big fan of British mysteries, comedies and dramas so it is no surprise that I am a fan of Masterpiece Theater. I recorded Poldark when it appeared on PBS and enjoyed the series, but did find it a bit on the slow side. I heard that there was also another “mini-series” done in the 1970s. I knew that both were based on a book so I looked it up and saw that the first book was published in 1945 (post-world war II) and the last book was published in 2002. I was really curious in reading Ross Po</span>
  <span id="freeText6458188073118304179" style="display:none">I am a big fan of British mysteries, comedies and dramas so it is no surprise that I am a fan of Masterpiece Theater. I recorded Poldark when it appeared on PBS and enjoyed the series, but did find it a bit on the slow side. I heard that there was also another “mini-series” done in the 1970s. I knew that both were based on a book so I looked it up and saw that the first book was published in 1945 (post-world war II) and the last book was published in 2002. I was really curious in reading Ross Poldark and suggested it for my online reading group. It won the poll so I was motivated in reading it.<br /><br />RATING: 4.5 STARS<br />1945 (Reissued: 2015); Pan/Sourcebook Landmark <br /><br /><i>"Cornwall, 1783-1787<br />Tired from a grim war in America, Ross Poldark returns to his land and family, only to find his father has died, his estate is derelict, and the girl he loved is engaged to another. But then he rescues a half-starved urchin girl and takes her home; an act which, it turns out, will alter his life."</i> <b>(From Publisher)</b><br /><br />I started this book thinking it would an okay family saga, but was really surprised on how much I loved this book. For me it was a bit like the first moment I read Outlander. I could reread this book a few time like I did with Outlander. it is because I really connected with this novel. The character development throughout the book was so well-written. You were given more than just a snippet of the person and their life. Throughout the book we would visit key characters and learn more about them this way. Ross is what I would call a "Bronte/Austen" hero in that he is brooding, flawed but also wants redemption. I liked him as a character and a hero. I was always rooting for him, but also had a bit of a crush on how he wants to help others. <br /><br />Graham is also great with the dialogue and interactions between the characters. It is through different characters that we also get the whole of who Ross is. His genuine affection for his cousin Verity shows his sensitive caring ways. You see the vulnerability and yet strength when he interacts with Elizabeth. I also liked that Graham did not turn characters in caricatures or one dimensional. Even the "villains" and "quirky" characters have all sides. I wanted to have constant hate-on with Elizabeth but you do see how she gets the way she does and I end up feeling pity for her. <br /><br />Books defined as "sagas" can either be angsty dramas, sex and gossip or really gripping portraits. Or it is for me. This one worked for me because it was well-researched in the historical time it took place. You didn't just get the sense of the time, but what was going on in those days - politics, social norms, courtships, war, etc. Ross Poldark has a great mix of drama, action, romance and history. It balances out perfectly so that you just really are entertained by a well-written book. I highly recommend you just try this book as it may be better than you think it will.<br /><br /><a href="https://mynovelesquelife.wordpress.com/2017/04/27/2831/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Novelesque Life</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6458188073118304179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9078101782980815500">KERMIT FLAIL: re-visit 2015 via new BBC series<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424293792i/13741357._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424293792i/13741358._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425839862i/13940370._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Episode 1 of 8: Cornwall, 1783. Ross Poldark returns from the battlefield to find his father dead, the estate in ruins and his sweetheart Elizabeth engaged to his cousin. On impulse, Ross rescues young urchin Demelza and resolves to forge a new life in the face of hostile forces.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425839862i/13940370._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Episode 2 of 8:Ross resolves to reopen his family mine with Francis. Demelza struggles to fit in at Nampara, and Verity makes an unsuitable match.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427057775i/14170963._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Episode 3/8: Ross celebrates</span>
  <span id="freeText9078101782980815500" style="display:none">KERMIT FLAIL: re-visit 2015 via new BBC series<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424293792i/13741357._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424293792i/13741358._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425839862i/13940370._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Episode 1 of 8: Cornwall, 1783. Ross Poldark returns from the battlefield to find his father dead, the estate in ruins and his sweetheart Elizabeth engaged to his cousin. On impulse, Ross rescues young urchin Demelza and resolves to forge a new life in the face of hostile forces.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425839862i/13940370._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Episode 2 of 8:Ross resolves to reopen his family mine with Francis. Demelza struggles to fit in at Nampara, and Verity makes an unsuitable match.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427057775i/14170963._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Episode 3/8: Ross celebrates the opening of Wheal Leisure as rumours spread of a scandalous relationship between him and Demelza. Francis and Elizabeth celebrate the birth of their new son. Ross must fight to save his friend Jim, sparring in court with Reverend Halse.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427659947i/14303423._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">4/8: News of Ross and Demelza's marriage spreads through the community, damaging Wheal Leisure's prospects. Demelza is filled with anxiety when Francis and Elizabeth invite the newlyweds to spend Christmas at Trenwith.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428265254i/14397654._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> Demelza gives birth and resolves to help Verity reconcile with Captain Blamey. Ross welcomes old friend Dr Dwight Enys to Cornwall, and Francis's persistent gambling threatens the security of all he holds dear.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428864626i/14488307._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> 6/8: With Jim gravely ill in Bodmin jail, Ross and Dwight launch a desperate mission to save him. Demelza is excited to attend a grand ball held by George, who is determined to ruin Ross and his smelting company.<br><br><br> Aidan Turner as Captain Ross Poldark<br> Eleanor Tomlinson as Demelza<br> Jack Farthing as George Warleggan<br> Kyle Soller as Francis Poldark<br> Warren Clarke as Charles Poldark<br> Phil Davis as Jud<br> Beatie Edney as Prudie<br> Alex Arnold as Jim Carter<br> Robert Daws as Dr Choake<br> Robin Ellis as Reverend Mr Halse<br> Heida Reed as Elizabeth<br> Ruby Bentall as Verity<br> Richard Harrington as Captain Andrew Blamey<br> Tristan Sturrock as Zacky Martin<br> John Hollingworth as Captain Henshawe<br> Gracee O'Brien as Jinny Martin<br> Harriet Ballard as Ruth Teague<br> Jenny Coverack as Connie Carter<br><br>I know, I know - no-one can replace Angharad Rees, especially not this scrawny tall piece of womenwork - but hey! let's give the lass a chance, think you? I'm all for getting behind her because she has a tough act to follow. ETA-Eleanor Tomlinson had won me over by the end of episode 2 - what a pushover I am!<br><br>But for those, like me, who whallow in the past here is some <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6KT7zf9EBfc" rel="nofollow noopener">Rees/Demelza footage</a><br><br>Bwhahaha - good spot by dear M - Robin Ellis the original Poldark is playing Rev Halse in this new edition.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379781093i/415353._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There are 347 pages in this edition. <br><br>phthisis = tuberculosis<br><br><br>A Novel of Cornwall 1783 - 1787.<br><br><b>Joshua Poldark died in March 1783. In February of that year, feeling that his tenure was coming short, he sent for his brother from Trenwith.<br>Charles came lolloping over on his great roan horse one cold grey afternoon, and Prudie Paynter, lank-haired and dark-faced and fat, showed him straight into the bedroom where Joshua lay possed up with his pillows and cushions in the big box bed. Charles looked askance round the room with his small watery blue eyes, at the disorder and the dirt, then lifted his coattails and subsided upon a wicker chair which creaked under his weight.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9078101782980815500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer18185268427180921757">Ross Poldark, how do I love thee, let me count the ways.<br/><br/>I had become enamored with the BBC series of Poldark. It is what spurred my desire to read the books that the series has been based upon. I have not been in the least disappointed with this the first book in the series written by Winston Graham.<br/><br/>In this novel, we encounter Ross Poldark newly returned from the war in the American colonies to find the love of his life, Elizabeth, engaged to his cousin, Frances, his father dead, and his estate </span>
  <span id="freeText18185268427180921757" style="display:none">Ross Poldark, how do I love thee, let me count the ways.<br /><br />I had become enamored with the BBC series of Poldark. It is what spurred my desire to read the books that the series has been based upon. I have not been in the least disappointed with this the first book in the series written by Winston Graham.<br /><br />In this novel, we encounter Ross Poldark newly returned from the war in the American colonies to find the love of his life, Elizabeth, engaged to his cousin, Frances, his father dead, and his estate in ruins. Ross takes on these challenges in a steadfast manner and faces what life has dealt him in a headstrong way. He attempts to overcome his love for Elizabeth while taking on the running of his estate as well as the mine that were part and parcel of the life and community of which he is a part. As time progresses he meets and hires Demelza a young girl so mistreated by her own father that she immediately finds happiness and solace as Ross's kitchen maid. <br /><br />Time moves forward for all the Poldarks and eventually Ross, because of a growing liking for Demelza marries her and takes on the job of raising Demelza up to his station. She provides for Ross a sense of solace and creates for him a felling of love and acceptance.<br /><br />Demelza, raised in such poverty and at a lower social standing than Ross starts to develop into a woman of character, intelligence, and most importantly of all, makes Ross become enamored of her.<br /><br />I am anxiously looking forward to the next book in this series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25365683.Demelza__Poldark___2_" title="Demelza (Poldark, #2) by Winston Graham" rel="nofollow noopener">Demelza</a> and the continuing story of Ross and Demelza and their love for one another, their land, and the people who are within their life's circle. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18185268427180921757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1913749592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15813179377409634748">Buddy read with some friends in The Reading for Pleasure Book Club. <br/>I had not seen the series on Masterpiece - but, I had friends who liked it. <br/>I joined the buddy read late. Everyone was already on to the second book. After I read some of the discussion I decided this might be something I would like, tho, it is not my typical read. <br/>All of that said, I am hooked and in for the remainder of the series. I just loved this. The characters are so well fleshed out. You really get to know them. My favor</span>
  <span id="freeText15813179377409634748" style="display:none">Buddy read with some friends in The Reading for Pleasure Book Club. <br />I had not seen the series on Masterpiece - but, I had friends who liked it. <br />I joined the buddy read late. Everyone was already on to the second book. After I read some of the discussion I decided this might be something I would like, tho, it is not my typical read. <br />All of that said, I am hooked and in for the remainder of the series. I just loved this. The characters are so well fleshed out. You really get to know them. My favorite character is Demelza. The second book, which I am on now, is her story. Basically, Ross rescues her as a 13 year old from a really bad situation. She comes to live with him and work for him. She is a survivor and has such a compassionate and loving spirit. I don't really want to summarize too much. I imagine others have done that. That is quite easily a 5+ star book for me. It is so rich and satisfying. <br /><br />I have now watched part of season 1 of the series and it is very well done. I highly recommend this book to anyone. Even if you don't usually read Historical Fiction - you will fall for the characters in this series and want to hear their story. This will be one of my favorite reads for 2017. So glad my buddies decided to read it and let me tag along. A very pleasurable read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15813179377409634748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1555095102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1555095102" />
    <a title="Lucia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia"><img alt="Lucia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484242793p2/8837962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1555095102?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucia" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia">Lucia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25170731-ross-poldark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555095102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1294852696804691356">Ross Poldark is historical drama/romance that reads as realistic historical fiction not as romantic chic-lit. It has very realistic feel to it, mainly because all characters are flawed, multi-dimensional and brilliantly written. I really liked that. I will take grey character over one-dimensional one any day. <br/><br/>I love historical family sagas and Poss Poldark is a promising start to Poldark series. I definitely plan t read next books very soon!<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5984709117355437049"><b> 4 Stars!! </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564421891ra/27906968.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ross Poldark returns from war expecting to be reunited with his father, and the girl that holds his heart. But thats not the case. His father is dead, and Elizabeth is engaged to his cousin Francis. Fast Forward a little and he meets a girl named Demelza who changes everything. <br/><br/>I love these books and the show!! Its absolutely right up my alley with political agendas and soap opera style drama. This is very much a word book.. and what I mean by that is that the wording and the way it i</span>
  <span id="freeText5984709117355437049" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars!! </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564421891ra/27906968.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ross Poldark returns from war expecting to be reunited with his father, and the girl that holds his heart. But thats not the case. His father is dead, and Elizabeth is engaged to his cousin Francis. Fast Forward a little and he meets a girl named Demelza who changes everything. <br><br>I love these books and the show!! Its absolutely right up my alley with political agendas and soap opera style drama. This is very much a word book.. and what I mean by that is that the wording and the way it is written, at times can be a little daunting but at the same time, so eloquent and beautiful. There were a few instances that the narrator changed or something would happen and I would get a little confused but for being an older novel it still packs a punch and delivers. <br><br>I fell in love with the story line and Ross. I mean really... ahem... how could you not?? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564422233ra/27906981.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br> Demelza- and that hair omg--- my favorite. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564422233ra/27906982.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love seeing her growth and looking forward to reading the next in the series!! <br><br>Overall im in love with this series and totally recommend the books and the tv show!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7casV67DTSaWfqKR7QZZgY95hNmQkRS1Qwsehh7vuLApsAgLamzeAVW05wn1P8LM/kvdi6h3XNrzvMnIWNJ76w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

E<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText6046055888898274045\" style=\"display:none\">Emma Marriott\'s The World of Poldark explores the characters, the compelling stories and the era that Winston Graham - and the television series - set out to recreate, the England that Ross Poldark returned to from the American War of Independence. England, and especially Cornwall, was then marked by social unrest and a deep division between rich and poor. It was a place of tin mines and shipwrecks, of new money versus old, of harsh justice and great kindness. And, above all, it was a place that inspired Winston Graham\'s beloved novels. Amid the turmoil of eighteenth-century Cornwall, Ross comes back to a home in ruins, his father dead and his childhood sweetheart engaged to another - his own heart as battered as the country around him. Experience the great houses and the glorious landscapes and follow the cast of characters as their stories play out against the backdrop of Cornwall\'s wild beauty, through interviews with the actors, behind the scenes insights and in-depth information on costumes, props and locations. Packed full of behind the scenes photographs, The World of Poldark is the ultimate guide to the popular series.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6046055888898274045\" href=\"#\" I soldati ci hanno dato un nome, come se fossimo un vero corpo militare: siamo Portatrici, ma ciò che trasportiamo non è soltanto vita. Dall\'inferno del fronte alpino noi scendiamo con le gerle svuotate e le mani strette alle barelle che ospitano i feriti da curare, o i morti che noi stesse dovremo seppellire. Ma oggi ho incontrato il nemico. Per la prima volta, ho visto la guerra attraverso gli occhi di un diavolo bianco. E ora so che niente può più essere come prima.» Con &quot;Fiore di roccia&quot; Ilaria Tuti celebra il coraggio e la resilienza delle donne, la capacità di abnegazione di contadine umili ma forti nel desiderio di pace e pronte a sacrificarsi per aiutare i militari al fronte durante la Prima guerra mondiale. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1782214842621147705">Winston Graham was the author of forty novels. His books have been widely translated and the Poldark series has been developed into two television series, shown in 22 countries. Six of Winston Graham's books have been filmed for the big screen, the most notable being Marnie, directed by Alfred Hitchcock. Winston Graham was a Fellow of the Royal Society of Literature (FRSL) and in 1983 was invested</span>
  <span id="freeText1782214842621147705" style="display:none">Winston Graham was the author of forty novels. His books have been widely translated and the Poldark series has been developed into two television series, shown in 22 countries. Six of Winston Graham's books have been filmed for the big screen, the most notable being Marnie, directed by Alfred Hitchcock. Winston Graham was a Fellow of the Royal Society of Literature (FRSL) and in 1983 was invested an Officer of the Order of the British Empire (OBE). In his death, he left behind a son and daughter.</span>
